style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Marcus_Aurelius" title="Template:Marcus Aurelius"><abbr title="View template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Marcus Aurelius</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#596;&#720;/: \'au\' in \'fraud\'">&#596;&#720;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'r\' in \'rye\'">r</span><span title="/i&#720;/: \'ee\' in \'fleece\'">i&#720;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/i/: \'y\' in \'happy\'">i</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#593;&#720;/: \'a\' in \'father\'">&#593;&#720;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'r\' in \'rye\'">r</span><span title="/i&#720;/: \'ee\' in \'fleece\'">i&#720;</span><span title="\'l\' in \'lie\'">l</span><span title="/j/: \'y\' in \'yes\'">j</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la">Marcus Aurelius Antoninus Augustus</i>; 26 April 121 &#8211; 17 March 180), called <b>the Philosopher</b>, was <a href="/wiki/Roman_emperor" title="Roman emperor">Roman emperor</a> from <span class="nowrap">161 to 180</span>. He ruled the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> with his adoptive brother <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Verus" title="Lucius Verus">Lucius Verus</a> (who took Verus as a <a href="/wiki/Regnal_name" title="Regnal name">regnal name</a>) until Lucius\' death in 169. He was the last of the rulers traditionally known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Five_Good_Emperors" title="Five Good Emperors">Five Good Emperors</a>. He is also seen as the last emperor of the <a href="/wiki/Pax_Romana" title="Pax Romana">Pax Romana</a>, an age of relative peace and stability for the Empire. His personal philosophical writings, now commonly known as <i><a href="/wiki/Meditations" title="Meditations">Meditations</a></i>, are a significant source of the modern understanding of ancient <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stoic_philosophy" title="Stoic philosophy">Stoic philosophy</a>. They have been praised by fellow writers, philosophers, and monarchs &#8211; as well as by poets and politicians &#8211; centuries after his death.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Early_life_of_Marcus_Aurelius" title="Early life of Marcus Aurelius">Marcus was born</a> into a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_patrician" title="Roman patrician">Roman patrician</a> family. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marcus_Annius_Verus_(III)" title="Marcus Annius Verus (III)">His father</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Praetor" title="Praetor">praetor</a>, after whose death in 124 Marcus was raised by <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Annius_Verus_(II)" title="Marcus Annius Verus (II)">his paternal grandfather</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Domitia_Lucilla" title="Domitia Lucilla">his mother</a> was a wealthy heiress. He was educated at home, as children from Roman aristocratic families often were, and later credited his maternal grandmother\'s step-father <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Catilius_Severus" title="Lucius Catilius Severus">Lucius Catilius Severus</a> &#8211; who helped Marcus\' grandfather to raise him &#8211; for his education. His tutors included the artist Diognetus, who may have sparked his interest in philosophy, and <a href="/wiki/Eutychius_Proclus" title="Eutychius Proclus">Tuticius Proclus</a>. Marcus was betrothed to the <a href="/wiki/Ceionia_Fabia" title="Ceionia Fabia">daughter</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Aelius" title="Lucius Aelius">Lucius Aelius</a>, his relative Emperor <a href="/wiki/Hadrian" title="Hadrian">Hadrian</a>\'s first <a href="/wiki/Adoption_in_ancient_Rome" title="Adoption in ancient Rome">adopted son and heir</a>. Aelius died in 138 and Hadrian chose as his new heir <a href="/wiki/Antoninus_Pius" title="Antoninus Pius">Antoninus Pius</a>, the husband of <a href="/wiki/Faustina_the_Elder" title="Faustina the Elder">Marcus\' aunt</a>, on the condition that Antoninus adopt Marcus and the son of Aelius, Lucius Commodus. Antoninus became emperor later that year, and Marcus and Lucius became joint <a href="/wiki/Heir_apparent" title="Heir apparent">heirs to the throne</a>. While imperial heir, Marcus studied <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>. His tutors included <a href="/wiki/Herodes_Atticus" title="Herodes Atticus">Herodes Atticus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Cornelius_Fronto" title="Marcus Cornelius Fronto">Marcus Cornelius Fronto</a>. He kept in close correspondence with Fronto for many years afterwards. Marcus was introduced to <a href="/wiki/Stoicism" title="Stoicism">Stoicism</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quintus_Junius_Rusticus" title="Quintus Junius Rusticus">Quintus Junius Rusticus</a> and perhaps by other philosophers such as <a href="/wiki/Apollonius_of_Chalcedon" title="Apollonius of Chalcedon">Apollonius of Chalcedon</a>. He was made a <a href="/wiki/Quaestor" title="Quaestor">quaestor</a> and the symbolic head of the Roman <i><a href="/wiki/Equites" title="Equites">equites</a></i> (also known as the knight class). He was appointed <a href="/wiki/Roman_consul" title="Roman consul">consul</a> with Antoninus in 140 and 145, the year he married Antoninus\' daughter <a href="/wiki/Faustina_the_Younger" title="Faustina the Younger">Faustina the Younger</a>, and with his adoptive brother Lucius in 161. On 7 March 161, Antoninus died and <a href="/wiki/Reign_of_Marcus_Aurelius" title="Reign of Marcus Aurelius">the two succeeded to the imperial throne</a>. \n</p><p>Marcus\' reign was marked by military conflict. In the East, the Roman Empire <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman-Parthian_War_(161%E2%80%93166)" title="Roman-Parthian War (161&#8211;166)">fought successfully</a> with a revitalized <a href="/wiki/Parthian_Empire" title="Parthian Empire">Parthian Empire</a> and the rebel <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Armenia_(antiquity)" title="Kingdom of Armenia (antiquity)">Kingdom of Armenia</a>. Marcus defeated the <a href="/wiki/Marcomanni" title="Marcomanni">Marcomanni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quadi" title="Quadi">Quadi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sarmatians" title="Sarmatians">Sarmatians</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Marcomannic_Wars" title="Marcomannic Wars">Marcomannic Wars</a>. However, these and other <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">Germanic peoples</a> began to represent a troubling reality for the Empire. Marcus modified the silver purity of the Roman currency, the <a href="/wiki/Denarius" title="Denarius">denarius</a>. <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Christians_in_the_Roman_Empire" title="Persecution of Christians in the Roman Empire">Persecution</a> of <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a> is believed to have increased during his reign. The <a href="/wiki/Antonine_Plague" title="Antonine Plague">Antonine Plague</a> that broke out in 166 devastated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Population_of_the_Roman_Empire" title="Population of the Roman Empire">population of the Roman Empire</a>. It caused the deaths of five million people, a quarter of those it affected. Marcus never adopted an heir unlike some of his predecessors; he and Faustina had at least thirteen children, including <a href="/wiki/Lucilla" title="Lucilla">Lucilla</a> &#8211; who married Lucius Verus &#8211; and <a href="/wiki/Commodus" title="Commodus">Commodus</a> &#8211; whom Marcus named as his co-ruler in 177. Marcus became the first emperor to die with a living, adult son since <a href="/wiki/Titus" title="Titus">Titus</a> succeeded his father <a href="/wiki/Vespasian" title="Vespasian">Vespasian</a> a century earlier, but Commodus is considered a disappointment as emperor and his succession has long been the subject of debate among both contemporary and modern historians. The <a href="/wiki/Column_of_Marcus_Aurelius" title="Column of Marcus Aurelius">Column</a> and <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_Statue_of_Marcus_Aurelius" title="Equestrian Statue of Marcus Aurelius">Equestrian Statue of Marcus Aurelius</a> still stand in Rome, where they were erected in celebration of Marcus\' military victories.\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#Early_life_and_career"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Early life and career</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Name"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Name</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a
